<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: -18pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">ITEM 1.&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;BUSINESS</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: -18pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">General</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: -18pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>North Central Bancshares, Inc., an Iowa corporation formed in 1995, is the holding company for First Federal Savings Bank of Iowa, a federally chartered savings bank.&#160;&#160;The Company owns 100% of the outstanding stock of the Bank.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s stock is traded on the Nasdaq Global Market under the symbol &#8220;FFFD.&#8221;</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The Company conducts business as a unitary savings and loan holding company and the principal business of the Company consists of the operation of the Bank.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s executive offices are located at the home office of the Company at 825 Central Avenue, Fort Dodge, Iowa.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s telephone number is (515) 576-7531.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">First Federal Savings Bank of Iowa</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The Bank is a federally-chartered savings bank that conducts its operations from its main office located in Fort Dodge, Iowa and ten other branch offices located in Iowa.&#160;&#160;Eight of the Bank&#8217;s offices are located in north central and central Iowa, in the cities of Fort Dodge (two locations), Nevada, Ames, Perry, Ankeny, Clive and West Des Moines.&#160;&#160;Three of the Bank&#8217;s offices are located in southeast Iowa, in the cities of Burlington (two locations) and Mount Pleasant. The Bank is the successor to First Federal Savings and Loan Association of Fort Dodge, which was originally chartered in 1954, and on May 7, 1987, became a federally chartered savings bank.&#160;&#160;The Bank adopted its present name on February 27, 1998. The Bank is a community-oriented savings institution that is primarily engaged in the business of attracting deposits from the general public in the Bank&#8217;s market areas, and investing such deposits in one-to-four family residential real estate mortgages, multifamily and commercial mortgages and consumer loans, with an emphasis on second mortgage loans.&#160;&#160;The Bank&#8217;s deposits are insured by the FDIC.&#160;&#160;The Bank has been a member of the Federal Home Loan Bank (&#8220;FHLB&#8221;) system since 1954.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, the Bank had total assets of $452.3 million, total deposits of $349.8 million, and total stockholders&#8217; equity of $49.2 million.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The Bank&#8217;s principal executive office is located at 825 Central Avenue, Fort Dodge, Iowa and its telephone number at that address is (515) 576-7531.&#160;&#160;The Bank&#8217;s website address is <font style="DISPLAY: inline; TEXT-DECORATION: underline">www.firstfederaliowa.com</font>.&#160;&#160;Information on the website shall not be considered a part of this Form 10-K.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Market Area and Competition</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The Company is a savings and loan holding company that conducts its activities through the Bank and the Bank&#8217;s subsidiaries to serve its primary market area of Webster, Story, Des Moines, Dallas, Polk, and Henry Counties, which are located in the central, north central and southeastern parts of the State of Iowa.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s market area is influenced by agriculture, manufacturing, retail sales, insurance, financial and other professional services and public education.&#160;&#160;The Company is headquartered in Fort Dodge, the Webster County seat, where it also operates two branch offices.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The year 2010 was an extremely challenging one for the financial industry and the entire world economy.&#160;&#160;The financial crisis and recession also impacted the local economies in the Company&#8217;s market area.&#160;&#160;The unemployment rate for the month of December 2010 for Webster County was 7.5%, for Story County 4.5%, for Dallas County 5.1%, for Polk County 6.2%, for Henry County 8.5% and for Des Moines County 7.3%.&#160;&#160;These compare to the national rate of 9.4% and the State of Iowa rate of 6.3%.</font></div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left">
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>
</div>

<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div>
</div>

<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">3</font></div>

<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
</div>
</div>

<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Prior to 2010, the Company originated and/or purchased loans (primarily one-to-four family, multifamily and commercial real estate loans) from outside the State of Iowa motivated by factors such as the type of loan demand in the Company&#8217;s overall market area, increased competition, and the Company&#8217;s decision to diversify its loan portfolio. During 2010, the Company curtailed its out of state lending due to declines in demand and management&#8217;s credit risk mitigation plans.&#160;&#160;Future opportunities for out of state lending for commercial real estate and multifamily real estate may be considered by the Company on a limited basis.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The Company encounters strong competition both in attracting deposits and in originating real estate and other loans.&#160;&#160;Its most direct competition for deposits has historically come from commercial and savings banks and credit unions in its market area. Competition for loans comes from such financial institutions as well as mortgage banking companies. The Company expects continued strong competition in the foreseeable future.&#160;&#160;Many such institutions have greater financial and marketing resources available to them than does the Company.&#160;&#160;The Company competes for savings deposits by offering depositors a high level of personal service and a wide range of competitively priced financial products.&#160;&#160;In recent years, additional strong competition has come from stock and bond dealers and brokers and, in particular, mutual funds.&#160;&#160;The Company competes for real estate loans primarily through the interest rates and loan fees it charges and advertising, as well as by offering high levels of personal service.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Lending Activities</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Loan Portfolio Composition</font>.&#160;&#160;The principal components of the Company&#8217;s loan portfolio are fixed-rate and adjustable-rate first mortgage loans secured primarily by one-to-four family owner-occupied residential real estate, fixed- and adjustable-rate first mortgage loans secured by multifamily residential and commercial real estate and secured and unsecured consumer loans, with an emphasis on second mortgage real estate loans.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, the Company&#8217;s total loans receivable was $341.2 million, of which $141.1 million, or 41.4%, were one-to-four family residential real estate first mortgage loans, $57.5 million, or 16.8%, were multifamily real estate first mortgage loans, primarily purchased by the Company, $69.3 million, or 20.3%, were commercial real estate first mortgage loans, primarily purchased by the Company, and $4.2 million, or 1.2%, were construction and land development loans.&#160;&#160;Consumer loans, consisting primarily of second mortgage loans and automobile loans, totaled $69.2 million, or 20.3%, of the Company&#8217;s loan portfolio.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Loans to One Borrower.&#160;&#160;&#160;</font>Savings associations, such as the Bank, are generally subject to the same limits on loans to one borrower as are imposed on national banks.&#160;&#160;Generally, under these limits, a savings association may not make a loan or extend credit to a single or related group of borrowers in excess of 15% of the association&#8217;s unimpaired capital and surplus.&#160;&#160;Additional amounts may be lent, in an aggregate not exceeding 10% of unimpaired capital and surplus, if any such loan or extension of credit is fully secured by readily-marketable collateral.&#160;&#160;Such collateral is defined to include certain debt and equity securities, but generally does not include real estate.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, it was the Company&#8217;s policy to limit loans to one borrower to $5.0 million, with higher limits subject to approval by our Board of Directors (&#8220;Board&#8221;).&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, it was the Company&#8217;s policy to limit loans to related entities, corporate groups, or common guarantors to $7.0 million.&#160;&#160;These limitations are more stringent than those imposed under regulatory requirements.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, the Company&#8217;s largest aggregate amount of outstanding loans to a single borrower or group of related borrowers totaled $5.1 million.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, the Company had no other lending relationship with an outstanding amount over $4.0 million.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

</td>

<td valign="bottom" width="9%" style="BORDER-BOTTOM: black 4px double; TEXT-ALIGN: right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman">198,079</font></td>

<td valign="bottom" width="9%" style="BORDER-BOTTOM: black 4px double; TEXT-ALIGN: right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman">319,262</font></td>
<td nowrap valign="bottom" width="1%" style="PADDING-BOTTOM: 4px; TEXT-ALIGN: left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman">&#160;</font></td>
</tr></table>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">One-to-Four Family Residential Real Estate Loans</font>.&#160;&#160;Traditionally, the Company&#8217;s primary lending activity consists of the origination of fixed- and adjustable-rate one-to-four family owner-occupied residential first mortgage loans, substantially all of which are collateralized by properties located in the Company&#8217;s market area.&#160;&#160;The Company also originates one-to-four family, interest-only construction loans that convert to permanent loans after an initial construction period that typically runs up to twelve months.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, 27.7% of the Company&#8217;s residential real estate loans had fixed rates and 72.3% had adjustable rates.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The Company originates loans for the purposes of both holding to maturity in its portfolio and selling the loans in the secondary mortgage market. The Company&#8217;s one-to-four family, fixed-rate, residential real estate loans originated for its portfolio are generally originated and underwritten according to standards that qualify such loans to be included in Freddie Mac and Fannie Mae purchase and guarantee programs and that otherwise permit resale in the secondary mortgage market.&#160;&#160;The Company generally sells fixed-rate loans with maturities of 15 years or greater in the secondary mortgage market.&#160;&#160;For the year ended December 31, 2010, the Company sold $50.4 million of one-to-four family residential mortgage loans, generally for the purpose of lowering the Company&#8217;s interest rate risk.&#160;&#160;One-to-four family portfolio loans are originated and underwritten according to policies approved by our board of directors.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Originations of one-to-four family fixed-rate first mortgage loans are monitored on an ongoing basis and are affected significantly by the level of market interest rates, the Company&#8217;s interest rate gap position and loan products offered by the Company&#8217;s competitors.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s one-to-four family fixed-rate first mortgage loans amortize on a monthly basis with principal and interest due each month.&#160;&#160;The Company also offers one-to-four family adjustable-rate first mortgage loans that adjust on an annual basis after the initial fixed rate term.&#160;&#160;</font></div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left">
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>
</div>

<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div>

<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">6</font></div>

<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
</div>
</div>

<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The initial fixed rate term of these loans are primarily five and seven years and the overall maturity of these loans may be up to 30 years.&#160;&#160;The Company determines whether a customer qualifies for these loans based upon the initial fixed interest rate.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: -0.2pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The Company establishes various annual and life-of-the-loan caps on adjustable rate mortgage (ARM) loan interest rate adjustments.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, the Company generally offered ARM loans with annual rate caps of 2.00% and maximum life-of-loan caps of 6.00% above the initial interest rate.&#160;&#160;&#160;At present, the interest rate on the Company&#8217;s ARM loans are calculated by using the weekly average yield on United States Treasury securities adjusted to a constant maturity of one year.&#160;&#160;In addition, the Company establishes floors for each loan originated below which the interest rate on the loan may not adjust. One-to-four family residential ARM loans totaled $101.9 million, or 29.9%, of the Company&#8217;s total loan portfolio at December 31, 2010.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The primary purpose of offering ARM loans is to make the Company&#8217;s loan portfolio more interest rate sensitive.&#160;&#160;ARM loans carry increased credit risk associated with potentially higher monthly payments by borrowers as general market interest rates increase.&#160;&#160;It is possible, therefore, that during periods of rising interest rates, the risk of default on ARM loans may increase due to the upward adjustment of interest costs to the borrower.&#160;&#160;Management believes that the Company&#8217;s credit risk associated with its ARM loans is reduced because of the annual and lifetime interest rate adjustment limitations on such loans, although such limitations do create an element of interest rate risk.&#160;&#160;See &#8220;Management&#8217;s Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condition and Results of Operations &#8211; Discussion of Market Risk &#8211; Interest Rate Sensitivity Analysis&#8221; in the 2010 Annual Report to Shareholders, which is included as Exhibit 13.1 to this Form 10-K and incorporated herein by reference.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The Company&#8217;s one-to-four family residential first mortgage loans customarily include due-on-sale clauses, which are provisions giving the Company the right to declare a loan immediately due and payable in the event, among other things, that the borrower sells or otherwise disposes of the underlying real property serving as security for the loan.&#160;&#160;Due-on-sale clauses are an important means of adjusting the rates on the Company&#8217;s fixed rate mortgage loan portfolio, and the Company has generally exercised its rights under these clauses.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Regulations limit the amount that a savings association may lend relative to the appraised value of the real estate securing the loan, as determined by an appraisal at the time of loan origination.&#160;&#160;The Company originates one-to-four family residential mortgage loans with terms up to a maximum of 30 years and with loan-to-value ratios up to 96.5% of the lesser of the appraised value of the security property or the contract price.&#160;&#160;The Company generally requires that private mortgage insurance be obtained in an amount sufficient to reduce the Company&#8217;s exposure to be at or below the 80% loan-to-value level.&#160;&#160;The Company requires fire and casualty insurance, flood insurance, where applicable, an abstract of title, and a title opinion or title insurance on all properties securing real estate loans originated by the Company through the Bank.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Multifamily Residential and Commercial Real Estate Loans</font>.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s loan portfolio contains loans secured by multifamily residential and commercial real estate. Such loans constituted approximately $126.7 million, or 37.1%, of the Company&#8217;s total loan portfolio at December 31, 2010.&#160;&#160;Of such loans, $81.4 million, or 64.2%, were purchased or originated by the Company and were secured by properties outside the State of Iowa.&#160;&#160;The multifamily and commercial real estate loans are primarily secured by multifamily residences such as apartment buildings and by commercial facilities such as office buildings and retail buildings.&#160;&#160;Multifamily residential and commercial real estate loans are offered with fixed and adjustable rates and are structured in a number of different ways depending upon the circumstances of the borrower and the type of project.&#160;&#160;See &#8220;Loan Originations, Solicitation, Processing, and Commitments <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#9472;</font> Purchased or Out of State Originated Loans.&#8221;</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>All multifamily or commercial real estate loans in excess of $1.0 million that are purchased or originated out of state are approved by the Company&#8217;s Senior Management Loan Committee as well as the board of directors.&#160;&#160;All loans less than $1.0 million that are originated out of state are approved by the Company&#8217;s Senior Management Loan Committee and ratified by the board of directors.&#160;&#160;Purchased loans are subject to the same underwriting standards as for loans originated by the Company.&#160;&#160;Before a loan is purchased, the Company obtains copies of the original loan application, title insurance policy, appraisal and personal financial statements of any guarantors of the loan, and certified rent rolls. A member of the Company&#8217;s senior management also makes a personal inspection of the property securing the loan. Such purchases are made without recourse to the seller. </font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><br>
&#160;</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;</font></div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">At December 31, 2010, $22.8 million, or 28.0%, of out of state multifamily and commercial real estate loans were serviced by the Bank.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, $58.6 million, or 72.0%, of the out of state multifamily and commercial real estate loans were serviced by the originating financial institution, mortgage company or alternate servicing financial institution.&#160;&#160;The Company imposes a $3.0 million limit on the aggregate size of multifamily and commercial loans to any one borrower for loans secured by real estate located outside the State of Iowa and a $5.0 million limit on the aggregate size of multifamily and commercial loans to one borrower applied to loans secured by real estate located in Iowa.&#160;&#160;The Company also imposes a $3.0 million and $4.0 million loan limit per secured property located outside and inside the State of Iowa, respectively.&#160;&#160;Any exceptions to these limits must be specifically approved by the board of directors on a loan-by-loan basis within the Company&#8217;s legal lending limit.&#160;&#160;See &#8220;Regulation &#8211; Regulation of Federal Savings Associations &#8211; Loans to One Borrower.&#8221;</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Loans secured by multifamily and commercial real estate generally involve a greater degree of credit risk than single-family residential mortgage loans and such loans also typically have larger loan balances. This increased credit risk is a result of several factors, including the concentration of principal in a limited number of loans and borrowers, the effects of general economic conditions on income producing properties, and the increased difficulty of evaluating and monitoring these types of loans. Furthermore, the repayment of loans secured by multifamily and commercial real estate is typically dependent upon the successful operation of the related real estate property. If the cash flow from such real estate projects is reduced, the borrower&#8217;s ability to repay the loan may be impaired.&#160;&#160;As a result, these types of loans present greater potential loan delinquencies and loan losses than single-family residential loans.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, the Company had approximately $5.3 million of commercial real estate and multifamily loans that were nonperforming, all of which were out of state.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Construction and Land Development Lending.&#160;&#160;</font>The Company makes construction and land development loans to individuals for the construction of their residences as well as to builders for the construction of one-to-four family residences and commercial and multifamily real estate.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, the Company&#8217;s construction loan portfolio totaled $4.2 million, or 1.2%, of the Company&#8217;s total loan portfolio.&#160;&#160;Construction loans to individuals for their residences are structured to be converted to permanent loans at the end of the construction phase, which typically runs up to twelve months.&#160;&#160;These construction loans have rates and terms which generally match the one-to-four family ARM loan rates then offered by the Company, except that during the construction phase the borrower pays interest only.&#160;&#160;Generally, the maximum loan-to-value ratio of owner occupied single family construction loans is 80% of appraised value.&#160;&#160;Residential construction loans are generally underwritten pursuant to the same guidelines used for originating permanent residential loans.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Construction and land development loans on commercial and multifamily real estate projects may be secured by land, apartments, small office buildings, strip retail centers, or other property, and are generally structured to be converted to permanent loans at the end of the construction phase, which generally runs up to 12 months.&#160;&#160;During the construction phase the borrower pays interest only.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, the Company had approximately $3.7 million in commercial real estate construction and land development loans which included a total of $3.3 million of nonperforming loans associated with four unrelated borrowers.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, $2.8 million of these nonperforming loans were out of state.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Construction loans are obtained principally through continued business from builders who have previously borrowed from the Company and from new or existing customers who are building new facilities.&#160;&#160;The application process includes a submission to the Company of accurate plans, specifications, and costs of the project to be constructed and projected revenues from the project.&#160;&#160;These items are also used as a basis to determine the appraised value of the subject property.&#160;&#160;Loans are based on the lesser of the current appraised value of the property or the cost of construction (land plus building).</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Due to the uncertainties inherent in estimating construction costs and the market for the project upon completion, it is relatively difficult to accurately evaluate the total loan funds required to complete a project, the related loan-to-value ratios and the likelihood of ultimate success of the project.&#160;&#160;Construction loans to borrowers other than owner-occupants also involve many of the same risks discussed above regarding multifamily and commercial real estate loans and tend to be more sensitive to general economic conditions than many other types of loans.</font></div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left">
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>
</div>

<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div>
</div>

<div id="PN" style="PAGE-BREAK-AFTER: always; WIDTH: 100%">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">8</font></div>

<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
</div>
</div>

<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Consumer Loans, Including Second Mortgage Loans</font>. The Company also originates consumer loans, which consists primarily of one-to-four family second mortgage loans, including home equity lines of credit. As of December 31, 2010, consumer loans totaled $69.2 million, of which second mortgage loans totaled $51.3 million, or 15.1%, of the Company&#8217;s total loan portfolio. The Company&#8217;s second mortgage loans generally have fixed interest rates for terms of three to five years. The Company&#8217;s home equity lines of credit are adjustable rate loans with terms up to ten years.&#160;&#160;The Company&#8217;s second mortgage loans are generally secured by the borrower&#8217;s principal residence with a maximum loan-to-value ratio, including the principal balances of both the first and second mortgage loans, of generally no more than 85%.&#160;&#160;In recent years the Company originated one-to-four family second mortgage loans with a loan-to-value ratio of up to 100%; however during 2008 that limit was reduced to 95% and in 2009 the limit was further reduced to 85%.&#160;&#160;Generally, second mortgage loans in excess of 85% loan-to-value are insured through a pool insurance product, unless the loan has secondary collateral.&#160;&#160;These types of loans are subject to stricter underwriting guidelines.&#160;&#160;As of December 31, 2010, the average principal amount of the Company&#8217;s second mortgage loans was approximately $24,000.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>To a lesser extent, the Company also originates loans secured by automobiles, with fixed rates generally up to 100% loan-to-value ratio for new cars. All of the Company&#8217;s automobile loans were originated by the Company and generally have terms of up to six years.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, automobile loans totaled $13.5 million, or 4.0%, of the Company&#8217;s total loan portfolio.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>In addition, the Company also makes other types of consumer loans, including unsecured signature loans, for various purposes.&#160;&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, other consumer loans totaled $4.3 million, or 1.3%, of the Company&#8217;s total loan portfolio. The minimum loan amount for unsecured signature loans is $2,000, the maximum loan amount for such loans is generally $5,000, and the average balance of such loans is approximately $2,400.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Commercial Business Lending. </font>The Company originates a limited number of commercial business loans, which the Company includes with its consumer loan portfolio for reporting purposes. Such loans are generally secured and are originated for any business purpose, such as for the purchase of business equipment.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The Company&#8217;s business plan calls for an increase in commercial business lending and deposit/cash management services to small businesses in its current geographic market.&#160;&#160;Commercial business lending will provide greater diversification of the loan portfolio in order to mitigate real estate concentrations.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; Loan Originations, Solicitation, Processing, and Commitments</font>. Loan originations are derived from a number of sources such as real estate agent referrals, existing customers, borrowers, builders, and walk-in customers. Upon receiving a loan application, the Company obtains a credit report and income information to verify specific information relating to the applicant&#8217;s employment, income, and credit standing. In the case of a real estate loan, an appraiser approved by the Company appraises the real estate intended to collateralize the proposed loan. An underwriter in the Company&#8217;s loan department reviews the loan application file for accuracy and completeness, and verifies the information provided. Pursuant to the Company&#8217;s written loan policies, at least one member of management approves all first mortgage loans.&#160;&#160;The loan committee of the board of directors meets quarterly to review a sampling of all loans originated in the previous three months.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>After a loan is approved, a loan commitment letter is promptly issued to the borrower. The commitment letter specifies the terms and conditions of the proposed loan including the amount of the loan, interest rate, and amortization term, a brief description of the required collateral, and required insurance coverage. Commitments are typically issued for 60-day periods in the case of loans to refinance, loans to purchase existing real estate, and construction loans. The borrower must provide proof of fire and casualty insurance on the property serving as collateral, and such insurance must be maintained during the full term of the loan. At December 31, 2010, the Company had outstanding commitments to originate $2.1 million of loans. This amount does not include commitments to purchase loans, undisbursed overdraft loan privileges, undisbursed home equity lines of credit or the unfunded portion of loans in process.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><br>
&#160;</div>

<div>
<div id="PGBRK" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt">
<div id="FTR">
<div style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left">
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>
</div>

<div id="GLFTR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div>

<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">9</font></div>

<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center">
<hr style="COLOR: black" noshade size="2">
</div>
</div>

<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic"><font id="TAB2" style="LETTER-SPACING: 9pt">&#160;&#160;&#160;</font>&#160;Purchased or Out of State Originated Loans.</font> At December 31, 2010, the Company&#8217;s loan portfolio contained $91.5&#160;million of loans secured by out of state properties.&#160;&#160;These loans represented 26.9% of the Company&#8217;s total loan portfolio at December 31, 2010.&#160;&#160;All of the one-to-four family, multifamily residential, commercial real estate and construction and land development loans in the Company&#8217;s loan portfolio which are purchased out of state by the Company are without recourse to the seller.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, the average balance of the Company&#8217;s out of state multifamily residential and commercial real estate loans was $678,000 and the largest loan had a principal balance of $3.2 million.&#160;&#160;As of December&#160;31,&#160;2010, nonperforming loans secured by out of state properties totaled $8.1 million.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>To supplement its origination of one-to-four family first mortgage loans, the Company also purchases first mortgage loans secured by out of state one-to-four family residences.&#160;&#160;Due to economic conditions during 2009 and 2010, including the uncertainty surrounding real estate values in other geographical areas, the Bank did not purchase any out of state one-to-four residential real estate loans.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, $7.3 million, or 2.2%, of the Company&#8217;s total loan portfolio consisted of out of state one-to-four family loans.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>There are certain risks with loans purchased by the Company that are not associated with loans the Company originates, such as risks associated with servicing of the loans.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, $18.6 million, or 20.3%, of purchased loans were serviced by the Bank.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, $72.9 million, or 79.7%, of purchased loans were serviced by the originating financial institution, mortgage company or alternate servicing financial institution.&#160;&#160;Although the Company reviews each purchased loan using the Company&#8217;s underwriting criteria for originations and a Company officer performs an on-site inspection of each purchased multifamily and commercial real estate loan, the Company is dependent on the servicer of the loan for ongoing collection efforts and collateral review.&#160;&#160;In addition, the Company purchases loans with a variety of terms, including maturities, interest rate caps and indices for adjustment of interest rates that may differ from those offered at the time by the Company in connection with Bank-originated loans.&#160;&#160;Finally, the market areas in which the properties which secure the purchased loans are located are subject to economic and real estate market conditions that may significantly differ from those experienced in the Company&#8217;s market areas.&#160;&#160;There can be no assurance that economic conditions in these out of state areas will not deteriorate in the future, resulting in increased loan delinquencies and loan losses among the loans secured by property in these areas.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>In an effort to reduce the risk of loss on out of state purchased loans, the Company generally purchases loans that meet the underwriting policies for loans originated by the Company although specific rates and terms may differ from the rates and terms offered by the Company.&#160;&#160;The Company requires appropriate documentation, and personal inspections of the underlying real estate collateral by a member of senior management prior to purchase.&#160;&#160;The Company limits its out of state loan portfolio concentration within a single state to 100% of the Bank&#8217;s risk based capital.&#160;&#160;The Company also limits its loan portfolio concentration to a single servicer to 100% of the Bank&#8217;s risk based capital.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Set forth below is a table of the Company&#8217;s out of state purchased or originated loans by state of origin as of December 31, 2010.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: times new roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline">Real Estate</font></font></div>
</td>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Loan Origination Fees and Other Income</font>. In addition to interest earned on loans, the Company generally receives fees in connection with loan originations. Such loan origination fees, net of costs to originate, are deferred and amortized using an interest method over the contractual life of the loan. Net deferred fees and costs are recognized into income immediately upon prepayment of the related loan. At December 31, 2010, the net deferred loan origination fees for the Company totaled $331,000. Such fees vary with the type of loans and commitments made. The Company typically charges a document preparation fee on fixed- and adjustable-rate first mortgage loans.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Investment Securities</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">At December 31, 2010, the Company&#8217;s investment portfolio was comprised of state and local obligations, mortgage-backed securities, collateralized mortgage obligations, U.S. Government agency securities, and corporate bonds.&#160;&#160;At December 31, 2010, $48,000 of the Company&#8217;s investment portfolio, was scheduled to mature in one year or less, $10.2 million was scheduled to mature within one to five years, and $38.2 million was scheduled to mature in more than five years.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 27pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Our investment securities portfolio is managed to provide both a source of liquidity and earnings. Our portfolio totaled $48.4 million at December&#160;31, 2010, compared to $23.2 million at December&#160;31, 2009.&#160;The increase was due primarily to the investment of increased liquidity generated by both deposit growth and reduced real estate loan activity during 2010.&#160;</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify">&#160;</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 27pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">We consider many factors in determining the composition of our investment portfolio including tax-equivalent yield, credit quality, duration, regulatory and overall portfolio allocation.&#160;&#160;Yield (spread to Treasury securities), credit quality and duration were primary considerations in our decision to increase our investments in collateralized mortgage obligations.&#160;&#160;All collateralized mortgage obligations in the Company&#8217;s investment securities portfolio at December 31, 2010 were issued by government sponsored agencies.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="left"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>At December 31, 2010, there were no holdings of any one issuer, other than the U.S. government and its agencies, in an account greater than 10% of the Company&#8217;s shareholder&#8217;s equity.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Sources of Funds</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">General</font>. Deposits are the primary source of the Company&#8217;s funds for lending and other investment purposes.&#160;&#160;In addition to deposits, the Company derives funds from FHLB advances, the amortization and prepayment of loans, the maturity and calls of investment securities and operations.&#160;&#160;Scheduled loan principal repayments are a relatively stable source of funds, while deposit inflows and outflows and loan prepayments are influenced significantly by general interest rates and market conditions.&#160;&#160;The Company uses short-term borrowings to compensate for reductions in the availability of funds from other sources or on a longer term basis for general business purposes.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Deposits</font>.&#160;&#160;During 2010, the Company attracted consumer and commercial deposits principally from within its market area through the offering of a broad selection of deposit products including noninterest-bearing demand accounts, interest bearing accounts, savings accounts, money market savings, certificates of deposit and individual retirement accounts.&#160;&#160;Deposit account terms vary according to the minimum balance required, the period of time during which the funds must remain on deposit, and the interest rate, among other factors.&#160;&#160;The maximum rate of interest which the Company may pay is not established by regulatory authority.&#160;&#160;The Company regularly evaluates its internal cost of funds, surveys rates offered by competing institutions, reviews the Company&#8217;s cash flow requirements for lending and liquidity, and executes rate changes when deemed appropriate.&#160;&#160;Public fund deposits totaled $27.3 million at December 31, 2010, an increase of $14.1 million from December 31, 2009.&#160;&#160;The Company also utilizes brokered certificates of deposit as an alternative wholesale funding source.&#160;&#160;As of December 31, 2010, the Company had $558,000 in brokered certificates of deposit compared to $601,000 at December 31, 2009.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Deposits are the Company&#8217;s primary source of funds. The Company may also obtain funds from the FHLB.&#160;&#160;&#160;FHLB advances are collateralized by selected assets of the Company. Such advances are made pursuant to several different credit programs, each of which has its own interest rate and range of maturities. The maximum amount that the FHLB will advance to member institutions, including the Bank, fluctuates from time to time in accordance with the policies of the Office of Thrift Supervision (&#8220;OTS&#8221;) and the FHLB.</font></div>

<div style="WIDTH: 100%; TEXT-ALIGN: center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">14</font></div>

<div id="HDR">
<div id="GLHDR" style="WIDTH: 100%" align="right"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 8pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160; </font></div>
</div>
</div>

<div>
<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Title Abstract Business</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>A component of the Company&#8217;s operating strategy to increase non-interest income is through the abstract company business conducted by a wholly owned subsidiary of the Bank, First Iowa Title Services, Inc. (&#8220;First Iowa&#8221;).&#160;&#160;First Iowa provides real estate title abstracting services in Webster and Boone counties of Iowa.&#160;&#160;These services include researching recorded documents at the county courthouse and providing a history of those documents as they pertain to specific parcels of real estate.&#160;&#160;This information is used to determine who owns specific parcels of real estate and what encumbrances are on those specific parcels.&#160;&#160;The abstract business performed by First Iowa replaces a significant portion of the function of a title insurance company.&#160;&#160;Iowa law prohibits Iowa insurance companies or companies authorized to do business in Iowa from issuing title insurance or insurance against loss or damage by reason of defective title, encumbrance or otherwise.&#160;&#160;Institutions can purchase title insurance for their own protection or to sell loans in the secondary market.&#160;&#160;First Iowa had nine employees as of December 31, 2010.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Insurance and Annuity Business</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Another component of the Company&#8217;s operating strategy to increase non-interest income is through First Federal Investment Services, Inc. (&#8220;First Federal Investments&#8221;), a wholly owned subsidiary of the Bank.&#160;&#160;The activities of First Federal Investments include the sale of life insurance on mortgage loans, and credit life and accident and health insurance on consumer loans made by the Company. In addition, First Federal Investments sells life insurance, annuity products, mutual funds and other noninsured products.&#160;&#160;First Federal Investments had five employees as of December 31, 2010.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Mortgage Company Business</font></div>

<br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>First Iowa Mortgage, Inc. is a wholly-owned subsidiary of the Bank.&#160;&#160;First Iowa Mortgage, Inc. originated first mortgage loans and subsequently sold those loans and the mortgage servicing rights to investors.&#160;&#160;First Iowa Mortgage, Inc. currently is inactive and these services are provided by the Bank.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Multifamily Apartment Buildings</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>On July 13, 1995, the Company formed the Northridge Apartments Limited Partnership (&#8220;Northridge Partnership&#8221;), a subsidiary of the Bank, with the Fort Dodge Housing Corporation (&#8220;FDHC&#8221;), a non-profit Iowa corporation formed to acquire, develop and manage low- and moderate-income housing for residents of the Fort Dodge area.&#160;&#160;The FDHC is controlled by the Fort Dodge Municipal Housing Agency, an agency chartered by the City of Fort Dodge.&#160;&#160;Northridge Partnership is a low-income housing tax credit project for certain federal tax purposes.&#160;&#160;A 44-unit apartment complex was completed on February 1, 1997.&#160;&#160;The tax credits for the year ended December 31, 2010 amounted to approximately $12,000.&#160;&#160;The final federal income tax credits amounting to approximately $12,000 associated with this project will be recognized in 2011.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>On October 24, 1996, the Company formed the Northridge Apartments Limited Partnership II (&#8220;Northridge Partnership II&#8221;), a subsidiary of the Bank, to acquire, develop and manage low- and moderate-income housing for residents of the Fort Dodge area.&#160;&#160;Northridge Partnership II was awarded low-income housing tax credits in 2002 by the Iowa Finance Authority.&#160;&#160;These credits were awarded to construct a 23-unit apartment building in Fort Dodge, Iowa, which was completed on March 31, 2003.&#160;&#160;The tax credits associated with this project for the year ended December 31, 2010 amounted to approximately $127,000.&#160;&#160;The tax credits will continue for an additional 2.3 year period.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Personnel</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>At December 31, 2010, the Company had 137 full-time equivalent employees (including the nine employees of First Iowa and the five employees of First Federal Investments).&#160;&#160;None of the Company&#8217;s employees are represented by a collective bargaining group.&#160;&#160;Management believes that it enjoys good relations with its personnel.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">FEDERAL AND STATE TAXATION</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="center"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">&#160;</font><br>
&#160;</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Federal Taxation</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">General.</font> The following discussion of tax matters is intended only as a summary and does not purport to be a comprehensive description of the tax rules applicable to the Company. For federal income tax purposes, the Company, the Bank and the Bank&#8217;s subsidiaries will be eligible to file consolidated income tax returns and report their income on a calendar year basis using the accrual method of accounting and are subject to federal income taxation in the same manner as other corporations with some exceptions, including particularly the Bank&#8217;s tax reserve for bad debts, discussed below.&#160;&#160;The Company and the Bank are not currently under audit by the IRS.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Bad Debt Reserves.&#160;&#160;</font>The Bank is a &#8220;large bank&#8221; as of December 31, 2010 and is no longer permitted to maintain a reserve for bad debts with respect to loans.&#160;&#160;The Bank instead utilizes the tax charge-off method for bad debt tax deductions.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Distributions.</font> To the extent that the Bank makes &#8220;nondividend distributions&#8221; to shareholders, such distributions will be considered to result in distributions from the Bank&#8217;s &#8220;base year reserve,&#8221; <font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">i.e.</font>, its reserve as of December 31, 1987, to the extent thereof and then from its supplemental reserve for losses on loans, and an amount based on the amount distributed will be included in the Bank&#8217;s taxable income.&#160;&#160;Nondividend distributions include distributions in excess of the Bank&#8217;s current and accumulated earnings and profits, distributions in redemption of stock and distributions in partial or complete liquidation. However, dividends paid out of the Bank&#8217;s current or accumulated earnings and profits, as calculated for federal income tax purposes, will not constitute nondividend distributions and, therefore, will not be included in the Bank&#8217;s income.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The amount of additional taxable income created from a nondividend distribution is an amount that, when reduced by the tax attributable to the income, is equal to the amount of the distribution. Thus, in some situations, approximately one and one-half times the nondividend distribution would be includable in gross income for federal income tax purposes, assuming a 35% federal corporate income tax rate.&#160;&#160;We do not intend to pay distributions that would result in the recapture of any portion of our bad debt reserves.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Corporate Alternative Minimum Tax.</font>&#160;&#160;The Internal Revenue Code (the &#8220;Code&#8221;) imposes a tax on alternative minimum taxable income (&#8220;AMTI&#8221;) at a rate of 20%. Only 90% of AMTI can be offset by AMTI minimum tax net operating loss carryovers, of which there are none. AMTI is also adjusted by determining the tax treatment of certain items in a manner that negates the deferral of income resulting from the regular tax treatment of those items.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Dividends-Received Deduction</font>.&#160;&#160;The Company may exclude from its income 100% of dividends received from the Bank as a member of the same affiliated group of corporations.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-WEIGHT: bold; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">State and Local Taxation</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-STYLE: italic">Iowa, Colorado and Washington Taxation.</font>&#160;&#160;The Company and the Bank&#8217;s subsidiaries file Iowa corporation tax returns and the Bank files an Iowa franchise income tax return, Colorado income tax return and Washington business and occupation tax return.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">The Iowa corporate income tax rate ranges from 6% to 12% depending upon Iowa taxable income.&#160;&#160;Interest from federal securities is not taxable for purposes of the Iowa corporate income tax.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 36pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman">Iowa imposes a financial institution franchise tax, in lieu of the corporate income tax, on the Iowa franchise taxable income of thrift institutions at the rate of 5%.&#160;&#160;Iowa franchise taxable income is generally similar to federal taxable income except that interest from state and municipal obligations is taxable, and no deduction is allowed for state franchise taxes.&#160;&#160;The net operating loss carryforward rules are similar to the federal rules.&#160;&#160;However, Iowa no longer allows carrybacks of net operating losses for tax years beginning on or after January 1, 2009.</font></div>

<div><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>Colorado&#8217;s corporate income tax is imposed on domestic and foreign corporations at a flat rate of 4.63% on net income derived from Colorado sources.&#160;&#160;The Bank is subject to Colorado income tax on interest income derived from loans, purchased or originated, in the state of Colorado.</font></div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt"><br>
</div>

<div style="DISPLAY: block; MARGIN-LEFT: 0pt; TEXT-INDENT: 0pt; MARGIN-RIGHT: 0pt" align="justify"><font style="DISPLAY: inline; FONT-SIZE: 10pt; FONT-FAMILY: Times New Roman"><font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 36pt"></font>The Bank is subject to Washington business and occupation tax for gross income derived from loans secured by property located in the State of Washington at a flat rate of 1.80%.<font id="TAB1" style="MARGIN-LEFT: 12pt"></font></font></div>
